<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_3916ba76-d556-48f1-bcf9-91c98da1e761'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1252459780759735925"><b>For fans of  <i>Matched, The Hunger Games, X-Men, </i>and <i>Blade Runner </i>comes a tale of a magical city divided, a political rebellion ignited, and a love that was meant to last forever. Book One of the Mystic City Novels.</b><br/><br/>Aria Rose, youngest scion of one of Mystic City's two ruling rival families, finds herself betrothed to Thomas Foster, the son of her parents' sworn enemies. The </span>
  <span id="freeText1252459780759735925" style="display:none"><b>For fans of  <i>Matched, The Hunger Games, X-Men, </i>and <i>Blade Runner </i>comes a tale of a magical city divided, a political rebellion ignited, and a love that was meant to last forever. Book One of the Mystic City Novels.</b><br /><br />Aria Rose, youngest scion of one of Mystic City's two ruling rival families, finds herself betrothed to Thomas Foster, the son of her parents' sworn enemies. The union of the two will end the generations-long political feud - and unite all those living in the Aeries, the privileged upper reaches of the city, against the banished mystics who dwell below in the Depths.<br /><br />But Aria doesn't remember falling in love with Thomas; in fact, she wakes one day with huge gaps in her memory. And she can't conceive why her parents would have agreed to unite with the Fosters in the first place.<br /><br />Only when Aria meets Hunter, a gorgeous rebel mystic from the Depths, does she start to have glimmers of recollection - and to understand that he holds the key to unlocking her past. The choices she makes can save or doom the city - including herself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1252459780759735925" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div id="review_926305211" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/926305211" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/926305211?book_show_action=true">May 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer926305211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13124711132167970955"><blockquote>
  <i>I’m engaged to Thomas and yet I let another boy kiss me. And I kissed him back. The worst part? He’s not even a regular boy—he’s a rebel mystic!</i>
</blockquote>Oh no! Of all the people suffering in the world, all the injustice going on in the Depths of futuristic Manhattan, THIS. IS. THE. WORST. THING. EVER!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399352249ra/9539532.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>That's great. That's wonderful. Good for you, sweetie. I just don't want your sort in a sci-fi/dystopian novel. Get the fuck outta here.<br/><br/>This book has<br/><br/>1. A weak, spoiled, wealthy TSTL socialite heroine who</span>
  <span id="freeText13124711132167970955" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I’m engaged to Thomas and yet I let another boy kiss me. And I kissed him back. The worst part? He’s not even a regular boy—he’s a rebel mystic!</i>
</blockquote>Oh no! Of all the people suffering in the world, all the injustice going on in the Depths of futuristic Manhattan, THIS. IS. THE. WORST. THING. EVER!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399352249ra/9539532.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That's great. That's wonderful. Good for you, sweetie. I just don't want your sort in a sci-fi/dystopian novel. Get the fuck outta here.<br><br>This book has<br><br>1. A weak, spoiled, wealthy TSTL socialite heroine whose attempts to do good are as laughable as a pet kitten bringing me a half-eaten mouse<br>2. A love...tri..quadr...hexa...thingamajig<br>3. A poorly conceived and largely nonsensical setting<br>4. A love interest with stalkerish tendencies<br>5. A plot that's 90% romance and 10% story, with not a single bit of subtlety<br>6. Villains that stand around twirling their mustaches and cackling maniacally<br><br><u>The Summary</u>:<blockquote>
  <i>Ever since I was a little girl, I have wanted to fall in love. The love you see on TV or read about in books, where you find your missing half—the person you were meant to be with forever—and suddenly you’re complete.</i>
</blockquote>It's the future, in Manhattan, New York. No idea when it is, but, uh, <b>"global warming"</b> happened and the world (the world meaning just Manhattan) has gone to shit. Yeah. It's <i>that</i> kind of a premise. Suddenly we have flooding and sweltering temperature and people with magical powers called <b>Mystics</b>.<br><br><b>Aria Rose</b> is about to have all her dreams come true. She is engaged to the son of a rival political family, <b>Thomas Foster</b>. Except it doesn't really feel that great. Why? She's lost all her memories.<blockquote>
  <i>I fought for true love, and I won.<br>Now I just have to remember it.</i>
</blockquote>Aria remembers everything. Her family. Her friends. The time she ate all those oysters and puked her guts out. It's just surprisingly specific that the one thing she can't remember is something that should have been the most important: Thomas.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399352249ra/9539533.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Hmm. HMMMMMMMMMMM.<br><br>Her upcoming marriage is a brilliant one. <b>Really, her forbidden (and forgotten) love affair couldn't have worked out any better for her family and Thomas'</b>. The Fosters and the Roses have been at political war for years, but now, they've decided to team up against a Mystic politician who is threatening their political dynasties. It's just the most amazing coincidence ever that Aria and Thomas has decided to fall in love at the time when it's most important that the two families ally together against a common enemy. It's just such a shame that Aria can't remember a goshdarned thing!<br><br>Hmm. HMMMMMMMMMMM.<br><br>Aria only knows something. There's a mysterious boy who makes her heart beat fast every time he's near. There's just something about him...<b>Hunter</b>. He's a Mystic boy, a forbidden boy who's as different from the patrician Thomas as night and day. Hunter shows up everywhere; her balcony, her room. It's just so amazing that he happens to be there every time Aria's in danger. <b>Like when she steps over a skyscraper railing just for fun, and almost splats to death due to her own fucking stupidity.</b><blockquote>
  <i>I’ve started to bring my leg back over the railing when my other foot slips.<br>And just like that, I’m falling.</i>
</blockquote>Ugh. Thomas is SO handsome, and SO rich, and it would be really nice to be his wife, and all her friends are, like, sooooo looking forward to their wedding.<blockquote>
  <i>The girls nod as if they understand. “That makes sense,” Kiki says. “Meanwhile, I still don’t have a friggin’ date to the wedding! I want some cute guy to dance with during the slow songs and make out with in the bathroom.”<br>“Time is tick-tick-ticking away!” Bennie says, clapping her hands together.</i>
</blockquote>But it doesn't FEEL right. Thomas is, like, soooooooo cold. And Hunter, is, like, SOOOOOOOOO HOT. <b>And then there's this pesky little thing about giving the poor downtrodden Mystics their basic human rights.</b> Which Hunter and Aria will TOTALLY get to. Once they stop admiring each other and going to carnivals.<blockquote>
  <i>From here I can see the entire carnival, the colors and the lights, the Magnificent Block ignited with festivities.<br>“This is gorgeous,” I find myself saying.<br>I think I hear Hunter say You’re gorgeous under his breath."</i>
</blockquote>Yeah. <b>Once they get their minds into the game and out of each other's eyes, Hunter and Aria will change the world!</b> How?!<blockquote>
  <i>“Love?” Hunter asks, his eyes wide. “Could the things you’re feeling be love?”<br>I gulp and nod at the same time. “I think so,” I say. “I hope so.”<br>“Me too,” he says. “More than anything in the world.”<br>Then he leans in and kisses me. Not on my forehead or cheek, but on my lips. A real kiss. A kiss that feels like it can change the world.</i>
</blockquote><u>The Plot</u>:<blockquote>
  <i>This is the first major event in eighty years that all the young Manhattan elite are attending together. Everyone will be here, regardless of allegiance—Foster or Rose, kids from both sides of the island. The plummet party at the American pales in comparison.<br>“Come on,” I say, shoving through a crowd of paparazzi.</i>
</blockquote>Because the best way to celebrate the union of two rival houses is to PARTY PARTY PARTY.<br><br><b>THERE IS NO PLOT.</b> The book SHOULD have been about Hunter and Aria working together to free the Mystics, instead, Aria spends 90% of her time going to parties, thinking about Hunter, hating her parents, thinking about Hunter, going to parties, wondering what's up with her memory loss, talking to her BFFs, thinking about Hunter, wondering what's the big deal with Thomas, going to parties, and thinking about Hunter some more.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399352822ra/9539643.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>The Setting</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>The heat, they say, is because of the global climate crisis, the melting of snow and ice around the world and the rising sea level that swallowed Antarctica and all of Oceania. Global warming is also to blame for the canals...filling what used to be low avenues and streets with seawater.</i>
</blockquote>Welcome to another "global warming" dystopian premise! With magic!<br><br>It's the future! We don't know how fucking far in the future it is, but <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Future_sea_level#Potential_to_exceed_one_meter" rel="nofollow noopener">it's gotta be pretty fucking far in the future</a> in order for global warming to get to such an extent to almost immerse Manhattan in water. The upper classes live in the Aerie, high-rise structures, while the lower classes live in the Depths, where crumbling buildings and shit falls on them all the fucking time. We now use gondolas to get around, and for some fucking reason, <b>the subways still exist</b>, but unused and sealed, but aren't flooded, since people still use them as hiding places...but why aren't they flooded, since they're underground? How did the waters recede in the tunnels, anyway?<blockquote>
  <i>I glance around at what must have been a waiting area for people to board the subway. The ground is slick with grime and eroded from where, at one point, it must have been completely flooded.</i>
</blockquote><b>Ah, logic. Fuck logic. Who needs logic anyway.</b><br><br>So in this magical, mystical future, <b>we have technology that can specifically erase memories</b>, but there's a surprisingly lack of technological advancements. Hell, it's like...the 21st century! <b>We have iPod-like music players, we have an iPhone-like device called a "TouchMe."</b> People still text and tweet in the future (Twitter will be happy to know they're not dying out any time soon).<blockquote>
  <i>“That stays between us, though. Okay? Don’t go texting it or tweeting or whatever it is you kids do.”</i>
</blockquote>We're still struggling to make paper records electronic.<blockquote>
  <i>The stack of manila envelopes on my desk has piled so high I fear it will topple over. Mental note: Get on those. They’re copies of the draining reports from over ten years ago, before everything was streamlined electronically.<i></i></i>
</blockquote>It's not like we're not doing that RIGHT NOW OR ANYTHING.<br><br>What the fuck kind of a future is this? Chanel still exists. It's too hot, if you step outside, you're practically boiled, but people <b>still take vacation to Bali.</b> Despite sea levels, people still seem to be able to eat the same kinds of delicacy, including seafood and oysters and stuff that might be impossible to get if the seas and the temperatures heat up? This book's premise is a mess.<br><br><u>The X-MEN</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>“Some mystics can take on the glamour of someone else,” Hunter says, navigating a flight of stone steps. “So you can look like a different person. But eventually it wears off. Other mystics can use their energy to affect the weather, or even the air surrounding them.” He waits for me to catch up. “I know a girl who can spin a tornado out of thin air,” he says, “and someone who can start a fire”—he snaps his fingers—“like that.”</i>
</blockquote>The Mystics in this book are fucking dumb. Supposedly they've existed all along, as witches persecuted for their crimes, and came forth to help the US during WWII. After which, they became DANGEROUS AND ENSLAVED AND DRAINED. Wut. Fucking really?<br><br>Ok, first of all, these Mystics are completely normal-looking. They're not X-Men mutants. They are humans with powers. They're just...hotter than others. They feel hot to the touch. And THAT'S why they were caught? Why can't they just fucking stay hidden? <b>If they've been so fucking good at hiding in the past, why can't they just do it again now?</b><blockquote>
  <i>“Pretending to be something you’re not sucks the life out of you. Even worse than the drainings.” </i>
</blockquote><b>Are you fucking kidding me?</b> You'd prefer to be almost enslaved, your powers drained, rather than HIIIIIIIIIIDE YO'SELF? What kind of a stupid reason is that?<br><br>Some of these Mystics have pretty fucking amazing powers. Why can't they just, like, <b>get the fuck out of there?</b> Seriously, emigrate to another country or something. Be Free like Willy. Some, not all, have powers that can make them look like someone else (glamour), they can control the weather, they can manipulate fire, they can walk through walls.<br><br><b>SO WHY THE FUCK ARE THE MYSTICS JUST LYING DOWN AND TAKING THEIR TERRIBLE TREATMENT WITHOUT A FIGHT?</b><br><br><u>Aria</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>It was Hunter. He’s saved me twice in two nights.</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399352822ra/9539644.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can't even count the number of times Aria got her ass saved. She's so fucking Too-Stupid-To-Live that it's unbelievable. <b>Here you have a pampered girl, one who is a celebrity, recognizable everywhere she goes.</b> She's got the street smarts of a dwarf rabbit, and she's sneaking around ALL OVER THE FUCKING SLUMS, and is OH SO SHOCKED whenever she gets caught (which is repeatedly).<blockquote>
  <i>“Please,” I say.<br>He licks his lips with his thick, wet tongue. “Please what?”<br>“Please don’t hurt me.”<br>I close my eyes, willing the pain to stop. I am going to die here. I am going to die for my stupidity.</i>
</blockquote>Aria is passive, to be fair, she can't DO anything because of who she is. <b>Aria is a spoiled-poor-little-rich-girl without an ounce of common sense.</b> it's not her fault that she was raised to be a smiling and brainless socialite, but I can and will hate her because I want a stronger character than that.<br><br>Aria doesn't DO anything. She doesn't need to work, so she halfheartedly holds a job at a local politician's office. Her days are filled with nothing but shopping and friends and parties (and thinking about how her life sucks). Her nights are filled with sneaking out to see Tyler. She can't even plan her own wedding, all Aria does is whine and sigh over how life is soooooooooooooo HORRIBLE.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1399352822ra/9539645.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>The Romance</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>“Are you spying on me?”<br>“Spying has such a dirty connotation,” Hunter says, running one of his hands up my back. “How about keeping watch?”</i>
</blockquote>Oh, here we go again, a boy who's a stalker, but <b>it's ok if he's stalking her if he's just looking out for her safety.</b> He shows up in her bedroom. He's there whenever she's hurt. He's there when he shouldn't be. He's not who he seems (remember, Mystics can wear other people's faces). <b>Hunter shouldn't be trusted, but the heroine seems to feel that it's ok to trust him anyway!</b><blockquote>
  <i>Something about him—his easy attitude, perhaps, or the way he looks at me—makes me feel I can trust him.</i>
</blockquote>As for the romance: <b>A is engaged to B (who is fucking C) while secretly in love with D (but shouldn't be) because D is secretly engaged to E, who graciously sacrifices everything because she loves both A and D.<br><br>*barf*</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="13124711132167970955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_461669452" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/461669452" />
    <a title="Lilian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7225730-lilian"><img alt="Lilian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453285003p2/7225730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/461669452?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lilian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lilian" href="/user/show/7225730-lilian">Lilian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer461669452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14652356841171502415">I need to stop being lured in by blurbs that mention The Hunger Games and sparkly covers (though it is one of most enchanting covers I've seen in a while.) A much more accurate blurb would be: a Romeo and Juliet retelling with magical people who are nowhere as cool as X-men. I didn't go into this book with high expectations, but I was expecting a lot more action (that wasn't made up of aimless running around) and a lot less love proclamations. <strong>In the end, I couldn't get past the extremely predic</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText14652356841171502415" style="display:none">I need to stop being lured in by blurbs that mention The Hunger Games and sparkly covers (though it is one of most enchanting covers I've seen in a while.) A much more accurate blurb would be: a Romeo and Juliet retelling with magical people who are nowhere as cool as X-men. I didn't go into this book with high expectations, but I was expecting a lot more action (that wasn't made up of aimless running around) and a lot less love proclamations. <strong>In the end, I couldn't get past the extremely predictable plot, flat characters, and the main character's stupidity.</strong><br /><br /><strong>This Couple Has OCD Issues:</strong><br /><strong>On two occasions, Aria finds these secretive letters in her house, then instead of stuffing them in her pocket or locking doors before anyone sees her reading them, SHE ORGANIZES THEM BY DATE. WHUT?</strong><br />Aria's lover, Hunter, isn't much better. When Aria and Hunter have minutes before the vicious, armed bodyguards barge into the room where they are having their secret rendezvous, instead of escaping, they proceed to sit around and talk...and talk...and talk some more. <strong>And then Hunter cleans up vomit.</strong> Y U NO RUN AWAY OR DEVISE SOME PLAN? They get caught. All because they were too busy talking and cleaning up vomit. *facepalm*<br /><br /><strong>Extraneous Writing:</strong><br />I often wonder if Lawrence forgot to remove his notes from the story since I kept coming across these <strong>jarring, filler moments.</strong><br />On one occasion, <strong>Lawrence dedicates an entire paragraph to telling us how Aria takes a bunch of clothes into her room</strong>, take the letters from her missing friend's clothes, then runs back to put the clothes back. Ummmm, girl, you could've just kept the clothes in your room and said you wanted to keep some clothes in memory of your friend...or you could even say the clothes would be a great addition to your closet instead of running back and forth between rooms suspiciously. I get it, you found these top-secret letters, NOW TELL ME WHAT THEY SAY. I don't care about the itty bitty details about you covering your tracks.<br /><br />On the other hand, she reads these secret letters she finds...then she eats dinner for a few paragraphs, then goes back to reading letters. No idea why that dinner scene had to be there unless eating stewed rabbit was a major turning point.<br /><br /><strong>Flat Characters:</strong><br />This was the main fault of Mystic City. I just wasn't compelled by the main characters, who were all conveniently "gorgeous." (Gorgeous must be Lawrence's favorite word.)<strong> Lawrence is much more concerned with describing clothes than people</strong> (you'd be surprised how many times he talks about flowing dresses and stylish clothes). There are no shades of gray in this story; all the "evil" people were all irrevocably evil, or suspiciously treacly. Everyone in this story LOVES to over-react and be drama queens. And <strong>Aria was the most gullible person ever</strong>, she never came to her own conclusions, instead she listened to people around her for confirmation. The only character I felt mild interest to was Davida, Aria's servant, and would've preferred the story from her point of view.<br /><br /><strong>They Also Don't Know How To Write Letters.</strong><br />Aria happens to find these love letters in her room which sound like they are written by an insecure, over-dramatic creep. The most hilarious one reads:<br /><blockquote>I have nothing to say tonight but thank you.</blockquote><br /><strong>If you have nothing to say, why are you writing a letter??</strong><br /><br />Or the letters are so blatantly unnatural that they made me wince. On another note, if you want to keep your letters a secret, you should burn them. If your friend can find them in less than five minutes, you probably weren't doing a good enough job hiding them.<br /><br /><b>WHY IS IT SO PREDICTABLE?:</b><br />Anyone would have guessed what happened to Aria in the first few chapters. The most frustrating part was how long it took for Aria to figure it out. Part of it was because the story is in first-person, so she's giving us all these hints that something is awry, but ironically, she's still completely oblivious. The plot twists were once again VERY PREDICTABLE. <strong>The foreshadowing basically handed us everything on a sliver platter</strong> (from who were the evil people and what those mysterious gloves are capable of.)<br /><br /><strong>Action?</strong><br />With X-Men, Bey Blade, and The Hunger Games in the blurb, I was expecting ACTION. And while stuff happened, it was mostly Aria running around aimlessly in dark alleys, trying to find clues to her past, but still ending up clueless...then SHE GOES TO WORK where she serves coffee and arranges files in a cubicle. *yawn* She doesn't need a job, <strong>she needs to get to school so she can learn some critical thinking.</strong><br /><br />Finally in the last few chapters, I get the action I wanted...except it suddenly turned into a bloodbath with decapitated people and body parts slewed around. Well <em>that</em> was unexpected, especially when the story was lovey-dovey up until that point.<br /><br /><strong>Romance</strong><br />Lawrence avoids "instalove" by maintaining the couple had a history before Aria's memory loss...but it just felt unconvincing.<br /><br /><strong>Book Trailer:</strong><br />One of the cheesiest things I've ever watched. Why do both guys have douchebag hair? And why do none of them look like teenagers?<br /><br /><strong>World-building:<br />Although I felt the story was lacking, <strong>the world-building is lovely</strong> (and maybe that cover had something to do with it.) A mystical city amongst the clouds--that's some lovely stuff.</strong><br /><br />Not sure if I'm having bad luck or I've turned into a nitpicker, but I've been on a roll with mehhhhh reads lately. If you want a sweet romance about a girl getting amnesia and waking up to a perfect life, read <strong>Sophie Kinsella's Remember Me</strong> instead. I don't know if I will be picking up the sequel next year; while I am mildly curious about the story, I just don't care about these flat characters.<br /><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />If Davida's gloves allow her to take a different personality every time, why does she need THAT many?? Won't one do the trick? And the more she has, the more chances she will get discovered, no? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="14652356841171502415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_461669452'><a id="like_count_review_461669452" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/461669452?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">41 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F13411245-mystic-city">Like</a></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1964669520" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1964669520" />
    <a title="booksnpenguins" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins"><img alt="booksnpenguins" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580407796p2/66222749.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1964669520?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="booksnpenguins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="booksnpenguins" href="/user/show/66222749-booksnpenguins">booksnpenguins</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1964669520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4285259400835987076"><blockquote>
  <i>Everyone around me is applauding wildly, overjoyed by how quickly something can disappear. Am I the only one who wishes things could come back?</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/><br/>Meh. This could have been better and the potential was all there. <br/>The book begins with a really impactful prologue that made my jaw drop, only to completely change direction when the story acrually started. Theo Lawrence can write if he wants to and that prologue proves it. Unfortunately for him, the weak rest of the book also proves that his writing,</span>
  <span id="freeText4285259400835987076" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Everyone around me is applauding wildly, overjoyed by how quickly something can disappear. Am I the only one who wishes things could come back?</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><br /><br />Meh. This could have been better and the potential was all there. <br />The book begins with a really impactful prologue that made my jaw drop, only to completely change direction when the story acrually started. Theo Lawrence can write if he wants to and that prologue proves it. Unfortunately for him, the weak rest of the book also proves that his writing, despite having its peaks, lacks continuity and consistency on the long run. <br />I think the setting is the only thing I have nothing to say about. I liked this new New York, and the Mystic caste system could have been developed more, but it was still easy to read and learn about so I'm not complaining. <br />There also were some seriously surprising moments that gave me hope, even if just for a second, that the book was finally going somewhere. Alas, it didn't last long, but it proves once again that TJ's talent exists, it only wasn't the right story to prove it with. <br />The plot is rather interesting if you don't take the self-indulgent romance part into account, or if you put aside the many and many plot holes (I fervently hope that all the things left unanswered in this book, will receive an explanation in book 2, because otherwise we're all doomed), but the characters are really dull and scripted. <br />The main character Aria is the one that irked me up the most. Seriously, how immature and ignorant do you have to be to make it all about your cheesy insta-love, when people are dying and/or in danger because of your family? Also, I get it that for the sake of maintaining a bit of mystery you have to make your protagonist (and reader) clueless to what's happening around them, but Aria was just plain blind, and also a little shallow if I'm allowed to speak in behalf of her judgy temperament. <br />Hunter, on the other hand, is a nice guy who tries too hard to be tough and probably hasn't overcome his <s>edwardcullen-like</s> stalkerish phase, but I didn't mind him as much as I did the others. I found him a little too sappy, though. Those love letters. <br />Omg, so cringey. <br />🙈<br /><br /><br /><br />Oh, I also really love that cover. It's what brought me to this book at first and, even if it wasn't a complete success after all, I'm glad I have this beauty to look at when I need something pretty to lay my eyes upon. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4285259400835987076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_261163524" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/261163524" />
    <a title="oliviasbooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks"><img alt="oliviasbooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1257619306p2/2843533.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/261163524?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="oliviasbooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="oliviasbooks" href="/user/show/2843533-oliviasbooks">oliviasbooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780375986420" href="/book/show/13414962-mystic-city">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Awaken (Kacvinsky), Blue Bloods (de la Cruz) and maybe Gossip Girl (von Ziegesar)</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=scifi-dystopian-apocalyptic">scifi-dystopian-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=witches-sorcerers-magic">witches-sorcerers-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=debut">debut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=love-story-romance">love-story-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=mystery-crime-sleuthing">mystery-crime-sleuthing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=urban-fantasy-paranormal">urban-fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2843533-oliviasbooks?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer261163524" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer108482076561896680">I would shelve <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5444795.Theo_Lawrence' title='Theo Lawrence' rel='nofollow noopener'>Theo Lawrence</a>’s young adult debut <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13411245.Mystic_City__Mystic_City___1_' title='Mystic City (Mystic City, #1) by Theo Lawrence' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mystic City</a> as <i>Futuristic Romantasy</i>, if I had to be precise. It takes place in a future, but alternative version of Manhattan. The plot relies heavily on its fantastic elements, namely on the existence of Mystics, who are people who have magic, which is used as energy, as the stuff which makes skyscrapers float high above the flooded landscape with its crumbling, moldy buildings, and as the basic ingredient of a wonder drug called Stic. And the st</span>
  <span id="freeText108482076561896680" style="display:none">I would shelve <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5444795.Theo_Lawrence" title="Theo Lawrence" rel="nofollow noopener">Theo Lawrence</a>’s young adult debut <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13411245.Mystic_City__Mystic_City___1_" title="Mystic City (Mystic City, #1) by Theo Lawrence" rel="nofollow noopener">Mystic City</a> as <i>Futuristic Romantasy</i>, if I had to be precise. It takes place in a future, but alternative version of Manhattan. The plot relies heavily on its fantastic elements, namely on the existence of Mystics, who are people who have magic, which is used as energy, as the stuff which makes skyscrapers float high above the flooded landscape with its crumbling, moldy buildings, and as the basic ingredient of a wonder drug called Stic. And the story definitely concentrates more on the stormy and unquenchable forbidden romance between the offspring of bitter, political adversaries than on the glitzy-glossy Mafiosi mystery. That tendency was more transparent in the novel's working title, which had been <i>"Your Heart Like Quicksilver"</i>. Like every other futuristic publication aimed at teenagers, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13411245.Mystic_City__Mystic_City___1_" title="Mystic City (Mystic City, #1) by Theo Lawrence" rel="nofollow noopener">Mystic City</a> comes pitched with a comparison to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2767052.The_Hunger_Games__The_Hunger_Games___1_" title="The Hunger Games (The Hunger Games, #1) by Suzanne Collins" rel="nofollow noopener">The Hunger Games</a>, which seems to be obligatory these days – plot and setting nonwithstanding – and which nobody takes seriously anymore. My pitch would have been "A cross between <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22188.Gossip_Girl__Gossip_Girl___1_" title="Gossip Girl (Gossip Girl, #1) by Cecily von Ziegesar" rel="nofollow noopener">Gossip Girl</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/872333.Blue_Bloods__Blue_Bloods___1_" title="Blue Bloods (Blue Bloods, #1) by Melissa de la Cruz" rel="nofollow noopener">Blue Bloods</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/576839.Exodus__Exodus___1_" title="Exodus (Exodus, #1) by Julie Bertagna" rel="nofollow noopener">Exodus</a>".<br /><br />I’ve rated <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13411245.Mystic_City__Mystic_City___1_" title="Mystic City (Mystic City, #1) by Theo Lawrence" rel="nofollow noopener">Mystic City</a> three stars, which means, I enjoyed reading it, all in all. There has been a lot of eye-rolling, a lot of 'Yes-Buts' and a lot of "Do-You-Think-I-Am-Dense", which I will explain shortly, but the heroine was thoroughly likable and brave, the hero attractive, super-powered and mysterious, the romance – although instantly there and super-kitschy – pretty romantic, the villains villainous, the action plenty and rapid and the world-building – although unbelievable – vividly painted in rich, sparkling detail and rather creative <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I want a rebellious boy fetch me from my penthouse balcony on his magic motorcycle, too. Maybe that would heal my fear of heights. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> - although I was a tiny bit disappointed about the lack of progress in communication technology: Mobiles are called <i>TouchMe</i>, MP3-players <i>AMuseMe</i> and people still use Short Message Services and E-Mail. However, my inner eye has been able to pull-up scene after scene and my mind has been sufficiently entertained and managed to stay on track until the book ended – on a half-cliffie.<br /><br />I do not want to gloss over the two major bothersome things I have hinted at:<br /><br />A) The predictability. I hate it, <i>really</i> hate it, when I am constantly quicker at grabbing the loose ends than the mystery-solving main character is, because everything is more or less obvious but continuously gets ignored by her, when I have to impatiently look behind me screaming “Come on girl, switch on your brains, morron. You’ve almost said it yourself a minute ago.” I had to wait until past the 50% mark for Aria Rose – who is <i>not</i> meant to be helpless Miss Clueless - to finally catch up and get a whiff. And <i>even then</i> it took her a <i>long</i> time to put the missing pieces of the jigsaw into the right places. <br /><br />B) The sloppiness. I think the author chose the easy road by integrating magic as a ecologic and economic factor into his or her post-melted-polar-ice-caps era tale. But that is perfectly acceptable. What<i> did</i> peeve me was that apart from some water in the streets and rather warm air the climate catastrophe does not seem to have changed the weather or the living conditions in a noticeable way. Aria’s parents suggest that she goes to Bali on her honeymoon trip, which had me thinking if much of Bali would be inhabitable then. Aria confesses to Hunter that she never saw a real tree or even grass before, which had me thinking where all the fruits on the Rose family’s table came from and how the air is still breathable. And finally, Manhattan. Manhattan’s buildings are standing 30 feet deep in water and the governors detonate unsafe buildings in regular intervals – upper-class people watch the destruction of houses like fireworks, champagne in hand. But the rebellion’s headquarters are <i>below ground</i> in abandoned Metro stations, where individuals have converted old vehicles into homes. How can that be? If living in the lowest floors of street level houses isn’t possible anymore, all Metro stations should to have turned into slimy, concrete-lined aquariums, too!<br /><br />I am not sure if I want to read the sequel, but I can say I had a rather good time tinted with a bit frustration and a little “Don’t-kid-me-and-don’t-shit-me”-vibe. And I really love that cover. The skyline, the darkness and the rich, delicate girl. It fits.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="108482076561896680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1566477579" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1566477579" />
    <a title="Emmeline Kazan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53260189-emmeline-kazan"><img alt="Emmeline Kazan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541553692p2/53260189.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1566477579?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emmeline Kazan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emmeline Kazan" href="/user/show/53260189-emmeline-kazan">Emmeline Kazan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53260189-emmeline-kazan?shelf=completely-adored">completely-adored</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1566477579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1196343988449349267">Amnesia. Tragedy. Tampered memories. Political ruses. Controlling and manipulative parents who treat their daughter as an asset to be traded to the most profitable buyer.<br/><br/>This book is... interesting? Not really in terms of the plot itself, but more the author's goals. Lawrence was attempting to create an original plot by twisting the storyline all over the place. And an alarming majority of these twists were extremely predictable, and foreshadowing was prevalent throughout the ENTIRE book. <br/><br/>Lack o</span>
  <span id="freeText1196343988449349267" style="display:none">Amnesia. Tragedy. Tampered memories. Political ruses. Controlling and manipulative parents who treat their daughter as an asset to be traded to the most profitable buyer.<br><br>This book is... interesting? Not really in terms of the plot itself, but more the author's goals. Lawrence was attempting to create an original plot by twisting the storyline all over the place. And an alarming majority of these twists were extremely predictable, and foreshadowing was prevalent throughout the ENTIRE book. <br><br>Lack of emotion was a frustrating approach that had been (intentionally? unintentionally???) taken by Lawrence, though for a reason I cannot fathom. If the narrative voice is going to be that of a female teenager's, perhaps she should have <i>slightly</i> more exaggerated feelings than that of a brick's. <br><br>She had indifferently told a lie, which had resulted in <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[her father shooting an innocent man for <i> supposedly </i> helping her traverse the canals of the Depths  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> and she had no compunction for this whatsoever. The meagre few sentences of her laughable dismay and guilt over this occurrence were unsatisfying. This event was an opportunity for Lawrence to truly showcase Aria's personality and give readers an insight to how she could cope with feelings of guilt or even rage, and he had missed the mark.<br><br>Throughout the course of this book, more significantly towards the end, Aria literally says how she feels ALL. THE. TIME. <br><br><i>"I always thought true love would sear me. Well, here I am—on fire, ablaze with love: my chest feels like it’s been broken open, my heart about to be ripped out and crushed."</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460951582ra/18807361.gif" width="400" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Beautiful, really. The emotion conveyed in those two sentences is the absolute highest standard of feelings in this book. But that's it. That's where it ends. <br><br>And of course, HOW did she fall in love? Because I do not remember reading about her <i>falling</i> into love, and/or of her gradual progression. Instead, the first time I read of her feelings was when she admitted to Davida that she 'hoped what she was feeling was love'.<br><br>Ummm. Excuse me, missy. How in hell did this happen? One second you are debating whether or not to trust him. Then you find yourself thinking about him. And then you assume what you feel for him in the span of days (!!!) is LOVE. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1460951582ra/18807362.gif" width="299" height="168" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Back up. What??? <br><br>This entire love story was flat, and we only learn of her sudden feelings during DIALOGUE. The advantage of writing a book in first person narration is that insight can easily be offered into the functioning of a character. Lawrence could have easily added in a couple extra sentences of Aria admiring her love interest, or her missing him when they are apart and emphasising on this often. <br><br>The romance felt rushed, and had it not even been there, the story would still have been as good as it is with it present. It literally made no difference. MY ALTERNATE IDEA: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[If her love interest had been her brother instead, she could have been secretly adopted into the Rose family. She then could have discovered Hunter was her blood brother, her real family, instead of the Roses who had adopted her for political reasons and the Fosters who only want her for her status to boost their own campaign. This could have also been a valid way to introduce whether or not she was also Mystic like Hunter, which could have been very effective in relaying to readers how Aria copes. We could have witnessed her struggle to discover who she really was and how to assimilate her abilities for combative purposes to protect herself, etc. etc.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>Character development also needed some work. I was not quite sure what to make of characters like Davida, Thomas, Kiki, Bennie and Turk. Though they were more or less background characters, they were people. People have lives, and issues and families, though none of these were communicated throughout the book. It was as though Aria only recounted what was relevant, and this adds an ignorant quality to her personality. Background information, despite irrelevance, is used to add depth and detail into how we interpret these characters and their impact on our protagonist. This information also cushions the action and plot by giving the readers further insight into the workings of society in such a different world to the one we live in. Lawrence could have played on this more to get readers to question our<i> own </i>world, too.<br><br>The plot, as aforementioned, was twisty and sometimes didn't flow or make sense because the storyline, much like the romance, felt rushed. However, the ideas explored were intriguing and original. For example, when Aria, Kiki and Bennie are at the Plummet Party, Aria comments on how they view the destruction as beautiful from a distance, and she questions whether she would think the same had she been standing at the site of demolition. This idea of 'beauty from a distance' piques interest and curiosity to this phenomenon and adds a much-needed philosophical element into this book. <br><br>Overall, the book had a decent foundation in terms of plot ideas, but needed work on the furnishings i.e. characters details, emotional depth, etc.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="1196343988449349267" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_412481301" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/412481301" />
    <a title="Dark Faerie Tales" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2766672-dark-faerie-tales"><img alt="Dark Faerie Tales" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1253675501p2/2766672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/412481301?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dark Faerie Tales" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dark Faerie Tales" href="/user/show/2766672-dark-faerie-tales">Dark Faerie Tales</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2766672-dark-faerie-tales?shelf=reviewed-by-kayla">reviewed-by-kayla</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer412481301" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16782966770821165478">Review courtesy of Dark Faerie Tales<br/><br/>Quick & Dirty: A girl tries to move on with her life after losing her memory, but moving on means being a puppet in a political race with her parents.<br/> <br/>Opening Sentence: The party has begun without me.<br/> <br/>The Review: <br/><br/>Aria knows she loves Thomas Foster. At least that’s what everyone is telling her. Loving someone with no memory of ever meeting them can be pretty tough, even if she does have flashes of memories — sneaking out late at night, meeting in the ghetto are</span>
  <span id="freeText16782966770821165478" style="display:none">Review courtesy of Dark Faerie Tales<br /><br />Quick &amp; Dirty: A girl tries to move on with her life after losing her memory, but moving on means being a puppet in a political race with her parents.<br /> <br />Opening Sentence: The party has begun without me.<br /> <br />The Review: <br /><br />Aria knows she loves Thomas Foster. At least that’s what everyone is telling her. Loving someone with no memory of ever meeting them can be pretty tough, even if she does have flashes of memories — sneaking out late at night, meeting in the ghetto area of the Depths, secret kisses… But then she meets Hunter, a rebel mystic that makes her forget her forgetfulness and the stress that comes with it. With a rising rebellion over the horizon and a mystic political candidate that could change life in New York for the worst, Aria has to decide which side she’s on — and which side she believes most. Should she let her parents use her as a political puppet to win the election? Or should she follow her heart — even if she doesn’t remember who she gave it to? This has the forbidden romance of Ally Condie’s Matched, adventure and mystery of Becca Fitzpatrick’s Hush, Hush and twisty plot of Beth Revis’s Across the Universe all rolled into one.<br /> <br />Mystics are outcasts — the ones who have the lower jobs and are never to be trusted. Yet at one time they helped build the city that is practically floating on stilts. But they became feared and thus the feuding Rose and Foster families took it into their hands to fix the mystic problems. So mystics are required to be drained of their power twice a year, leaving them as shells of their old self. But a rebellion is brewing of undrained mystics and even a union between a Rose and a Foster might not distract the citizens.<br /> <br />I think I’ve found my new favorite series. Imagine Silence by Becca Fitzpatrick as the first book in the series and you’ve pretty much got Mystic City in a nutshell. We don’t know Aria’s past and we don’t know about the dystopian world of Mystics and Aeries. Lawrence weaves an intriguing mystery full of action and suspense and pretty much everything you want in a YA dystopian book.<br /> <br />Hunter…oh my. He’s charming, sweet, and can knock a girl off her feet if he really tried. But he has his own secrets and obstacles to overcome. He thinks he’s doing the right thing by staying away from Aria, keeping her from danger and letting her live her life of high-end, classy materials. He’s strong not just physically but also mentally for having to endure the trials (sorry for being vague–can’t spoil the story!).<br /> <br />There were multiple consistency problems but that’s due to it being an ARC…but the fabulous writing and unpredictable plot makes up for it. The entire cast of characters are great in themselves, but I thought some of the minor characters could have been mentioned earlier in the story. Manhattan as a dystopian city is absolutely beautiful and can (and will) steal your breath away. Overall this has great potential and Lawrence will definitely be on my “debut-author-to-be-watched” list. I can’t wait until the next installment! (But first I got to wait for this book to come out…)<br /> <br />Notable Scene: <br /><br />So little time is left.<br /> <br />“Take this.” He folds the locket into my hand. It throbs as if it has a pulse, giving off a faint white glow. “I’m sorry for putting you in danger.”<br /> <br />“I would do it all again,” I tell him. “A thousand times.”<br /> <br />He kisses me, softly at first, and then so fiercely I can hardly breathe. Rain falls, soaking us, splashing into the canals that twist through the hot, dark city. His chest heaves against mine. The sound of sirens–and gunshots–reverberates between the crumbling, waterlogged buildings.<br /> <br />My family is drawing closer.<br /> <br />“Go, Aria,” he pleads. “Before they get here.”<br /> <br />But footsteps are behind me now. Voices fill my ears. Fingers dig into my arms, tearing me away.<br /> <br />“I love you,” he says gently.<br /> <br />And then they take him. I scream in defiance, but it is too late.<br /> <br />My father emerges from the shadows. He aims the wicked barrel of his pistol at my head.<br /> <br />Inside me, something bursts.<br /> <br />I always knew this story would break my heart.<br /><br />FTC Advisory: Delacorte Books for Young Readers/Random House provided me with a copy of Mystic City. No goody bags, sponsorships, “material connections,” or bribes were exchanged for my review.</span>

<div id="review_358148965" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/358148965" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/358148965?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=apocalyptic-dystopian">apocalyptic-dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss">netgalley-edelweiss</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer358148965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8264014232886180922">3.5 stars<br/><br/><b>Mystic City</b> has just about everything one would enjoy in an escape. It's has a quaint Romeo and Juliet story line, a political background, a sci-fi flare and magic laced in every page. Add conspiracy, betrayal, true love and tainted memory lost and how could you go wrong?<br/><br/>Theo Lawrence pens a brilliant imaginative and creative world. It's set in a futuristic Manhattan and there are two kinds of people. One are the Mystics who have special powers and forces of energy. They are meant to be</span>
  <span id="freeText8264014232886180922" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br><br><b>Mystic City</b> has just about everything one would enjoy in an escape. It's has a quaint Romeo and Juliet story line, a political background, a sci-fi flare and magic laced in every page. Add conspiracy, betrayal, true love and tainted memory lost and how could you go wrong?<br><br>Theo Lawrence pens a brilliant imaginative and creative world. It's set in a futuristic Manhattan and there are two kinds of people. One are the Mystics who have special powers and forces of energy. They are meant to be dangerous and a nuisance to the Non-Mystic folks. Aria Rose just happens to be the daughter of a very important political family. She is the key to bringing peace to their country by joining two rival families together through marriage...but only if she doesn't remember enough of who she really loves.<br><br>I loved the idea that Theo Lawrence introduced. Always was a sucker for amnesia type books and this one had a really great twist. I also loved the magic in this. It truly did give a mystical feel to the whole story-line giving it an enchanting glow. And while politics usually leaves me cold, it was easy to understand and go along with. Even the romance was sweet in it's own way. <br>So why only three stars you might wonder? I'm thinking it has to do with the pacing and the fact that it just was way to predictable. The flow of the book felt a tad off. We start off with Aria at her engagement party but she doesn't remember who her fiance is or feel the love she's suppose to have for him. Then almost in the same breath she's saved from someone who she feels instantly connected too. It felt to fast to give out such important facts right from the start. Invading any real mystery from then on.<br>It also wasn't hard to guess the intentions of the characters. Who was bad, who was good and the why's of the situation. Making it feel somewhat lacking.<br><br>However, I did enjoy all the characters. I felt badly for Aria. She's been used and betrayed through out the entire story and yet she has quite a fiery determination about her that you just have to respect.<br>Hunter is the kind of character that's funny and sweet and playful. Someone you can feel like you can trust right away but you also know that there is more to him. <br>The romance wasn't over the top in this book, but it still had it's moments where I couldn't help but sigh.<br>Also, I'm not sure why, but I felt badly for Thomas, even though he was partly at fault, he wasn't a bad guy and I'm not sure he deserved what he got.<br><br>With that said, all in all, I still enjoyed this story. It may not be a favorite, but I still think it was a fascinating read. The writing is good, the characters are likable and the plot was intriguing. Lawrence brings something shinny and bright into the world of dystopian reads. The ending actually has me curious enough to want to know what happens next, so I may have to pick up the next book;<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16085468.Renegade_Heart__Mystic_City___2_" title="Renegade Heart (Mystic City, #2) by Theo Lawrence" rel="nofollow noopener">Renegade Heart</a><br><br>This review and more can be seen at; WinterHaven Books!<br><br><a href="http://www.winterhavenbooks.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333076i/693179.png" alt="winter haven books" width="150" height="111" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8264014232886180922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/434831338" />
    <a title="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd"><img alt="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382576238p2/8096484.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/434831338?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)" href="/user/show/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd">Jessica (The Psychotic Nerd)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=series-books">series-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=dystopian-and-post-apocalyptic">dystopian-and-post-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=hall-of-awesome-4-stars-or-more">hall-of-awesome-4-stars-or-more</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=pov-girl">pov-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=penguin-random-house">penguin-random-house</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=witches-magic-and-more">witches-magic-and-more</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8096484-jessica-the-psychotic-nerd?shelf=released-in-2012">released-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer434831338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5281031303625153165">This and other reviews can be found on <a href='http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Psychotic Nerd</a><br/><br/><b>
  <u>MY THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br/>I've been wanting to read this book for awhile, so I felt like I hit the jackpot when I found this book and it's sequel at my local used bookstore! Overall, this book did not disappoint!<br/><br/>This book take place in a futuristic/dystopian New York City. There are two ruling families, the Roses and the Fosters, and everyone in the city has to choose sides between them. Aria has just 'recovered' after ODing off of Stix (a drug) and </span>
  <span id="freeText5281031303625153165" style="display:none">This and other reviews can be found on <a href="http://thepsychoticnerd.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Psychotic Nerd</a><br /><br /><b>
  <u>MY THOUGHTS</u>
</b><br />I've been wanting to read this book for awhile, so I felt like I hit the jackpot when I found this book and it's sequel at my local used bookstore! Overall, this book did not disappoint!<br /><br />This book take place in a futuristic/dystopian New York City. There are two ruling families, the Roses and the Fosters, and everyone in the city has to choose sides between them. Aria has just 'recovered' after ODing off of Stix (a drug) and is now to marry Thomas Foster, whom she supposedly loves and had a great affair with. The problem is that she has no memory of being with Thomas and has no love for him. She ends of meeting Hunter, a mysterious illegal mystic (has magical abilities). She knows that with he she will be able to recall her memories, but what she will unlock will change everything.<br /><br />This entire plot was just so interesting! I like the whole idea behind the two families and the mystics. It's horrible how they treat the mystics, they drain their powers, but I thought the idea of adding magical elements to a dystopian society very unique. This book has the common theme of everything I was told is a lie, but it's so well done. The element of memory loss is not something you see entirely too often with that idea either. <br /><br />As for plot,some parts of this book were very predictable. I was able to figure most of the plot early on, though I won't hate on Aria for taking so long to figure things out, as it probably comes from reading so many dystopian novels. Even though, I still very thrown by a few plot twists near the end! The pacing of the book was also fast-paced. You wouldn't expect that with a book featuring memory loss, but there were always things happening and Aria did not just wait around for her memories to come back!<br /><br />The romance was very different, in some ways. It seems like there would be a love triangle in this book, but there really isn't, since Aria doesn't really love one of them. If you are one of those people who avoids books with two guy names in the synopsis, expecting the dreaded triangle, you'll be safe reading this book! As for everything else in the romance, I liked it, though it didn't wow me. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>IN CONCLUSION</u>
</b><br />This is a great read with a very interesting premise and it's done very well! It's a bit predictable at times, but I didn't let that stop my enjoyment of the book and there were still some surprises along the way! I recommend this book to those who would like to read a dystopian with a hint of fantasy, meanwhile, I'll be reading the next book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5281031303625153165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_425517957" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/425517957" />
    <a title="Katy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4572741-katy"><img alt="Katy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365039295p2/4572741.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/425517957?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katy" href="/user/show/4572741-katy">Katy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer425517957" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14490550134947310443">This book had such an interesting premise, and I was really looking forward to it, but overall, it was <b>
  <u>disappointingly just okay.</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Predictable</u>
</b> - Sadly, I was able to guess what was going to happen after reading the first couple of chapters. I mean, yes, I had an idea from the summary, but this book <b>
  <u>did not have any twists or turns or any surprises with one exception</u>
</b> - the kiss did make me think "WTH," but that was it. I guessed what was really going on, the whole romance thing, who was</span>
  <span id="freeText14490550134947310443" style="display:none">This book had such an interesting premise, and I was really looking forward to it, but overall, it was <b>
  <u>disappointingly just okay.</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Predictable</u>
</b> - Sadly, I was able to guess what was going to happen after reading the first couple of chapters. I mean, yes, I had an idea from the summary, but this book <b>
  <u>did not have any twists or turns or any surprises with one exception</u>
</b> - the kiss did make me think "WTH," but that was it. I guessed what was really going on, the whole romance thing, who was related to who, and whose side each character was on (so no, the revealing of the spies did not surprise me either).<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Fuzzy World Building</u>
</b> - I really liked that Lawrence started to establish a concept of the world of mystics, the magic and the levels of sociology and even where the lived. BUT it was just the initial set up. The world was sci-fi-ish, but I had a <b>
  <u>really hard time picturing everything</u>
</b> - how the world was set up, how people got around other than walk, what Aeries looks like, what the Mystics' underground or whatever looked like.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Lack of Building on Magic</u>
</b> - Lawrence had so much he could have done on with the concept of magic, but it he <b>
  <u>never really built on it.</u>
</b> It was just thrown in and accepted like it was always a part of history, and other than the little anecdote about Hunter's grandfather and mother, there wasn't much on how mystics contributed to the world and why they were not accepted into society other than people were afraid of their power. And the powers themselves? They were pretty lame, and their users did not do much with them - other than the ultimate traitor.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Unimpressive characters</u>
</b> - The characters in this book were just okay, and honestly, <b>
  <u>they're very forgettable.</u>
</b> Aria was kind of bland. I'm sure she was meant to be a rebellious, feisty character, but she really didn't do much other than show a little fight near the end. Hunter was kind of sappy, and I'm disappointed he wasn't built to be more of a swoony-worthy character.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>I was unattached to any of the side characters.</u>
</b> I really wanted to know more about Kyle, who was supposed to be such a good brother; or Kiki and Bennie, who was supposedly Aria's really good friends; or even Turk, who would have been a really fun character to get to know. Lawrence did show us a <b>
  <u>glimpse of Davida, but it was so quick,</u>
</b> and I think she would have been a really, really strong supporting character.<br /><br />Overall, I don't think this book was a bad book, per se. It's just that for a 416-paged book, <b>
  <u>I just felt a lot of it was a brief gloss-over, and I had just expected it to be more attached to the story, the characters and the world.</u>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14490550134947310443" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
