<div id="review_320443814" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/320443814" />
    <a title="Annabelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1235083-annabelle"><img alt="Annabelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348368292p2/1235083.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/320443814?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annabelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annabelle" href="/user/show/1235083-annabelle">Annabelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780375986420" href="/book/show/13414962-mystic-city">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=wtf-is-this">wtf-is-this</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1235083-annabelle?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer320443814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15801530510584824087">**FINAL RATING: 2.00 STARS**<br/><br/><b>
  <u>CATCHALL</u>
</b><br/>So, despite all the mixed reviews I saw this book getting, I was reasonably certain that I'd love it. I was so, so wrong. Obviously I need to stop being shallow and being drawn in by tempting blurbs and shiny, shiny covers that look like tiny pieces of heaven. I even read the first fifty pages in the bookstore and really enjoyed it. Unfortunately, that was pretty much the best part of the book. Unfortunately, it was downhill from there.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>THE HEROINE</u>
</b><br/><u>ARIA</u><br/>A</span>
  <span id="freeText15801530510584824087" style="display:none">**FINAL RATING: 2.00 STARS**<br /><br /><b>
  <u>CATCHALL</u>
</b><br />So, despite all the mixed reviews I saw this book getting, I was reasonably certain that I'd love it. I was so, so wrong. Obviously I need to stop being shallow and being drawn in by tempting blurbs and shiny, shiny covers that look like tiny pieces of heaven. I even read the first fifty pages in the bookstore and really enjoyed it. Unfortunately, that was pretty much the best part of the book. Unfortunately, it was downhill from there.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE HEROINE</u>
</b><br /><u>ARIA</u><br />Aria has got to be one of the most irritating heroines in the history of YA. She's constantly doing stupid things even though she knows she shouldn't, and she's possibly one of the densest people ever. She doesn't notice all these obvious clues around her, and when she does she completely misinterprets them. She just doesn't go about things in a smart way at all and she also seems to have split personality, sometimes the perfect daughter and others the daring rebel. No in between. It's really not charming.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE LOVE INTEREST</u>
</b><br /><u>HUNTER</u><br />I don't hate Hunter, but that's probably because there's nothing to hate. He's a very flat character who lacks substance and there just isn't much to him at all. He's a rebel. He has a ton of secrets. Other than that, he basically just exists. It's fascinating stuff.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE PLOT</u>
</b><br />Now, don't get me wrong: I liked Mystic City. However, I also like rainbows and colorful butterflies. "Like" isn't a word I apply a ton of value to. It could have been interesting, but the execution was just embarrassing.<br /><br />It's so predictable. From almost the very beginning, I could tell you exactly where the story was going. Sure, I didn't get every detail. But the main plot? Way. Too. Predictable. I don't want to know the ending before I even get halfway through the book. It's annoying.<br /><br />There are lots of "subtle hints" dropped throughout the book that–you guessed it–are in fact not subtle at all. It was a huge disappointment, and I seriously did not understand how anyone could have thought that they weren't glaringly obvious.<br /><br />Plot holes. Oh my god, plot holes everywhere. And please don't get me started on Aria's stupid decisions. I swear at least half of the book is Hunter saving her from her own idiocy. That's all right to a point but it quickly became old.<br /><br />The story was, however, entertaining. I'm not a liar, and that's a fact. But that doesn't change the fact that it was still faulty in too many areas to overlook.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE ROMANCE</u>
</b><br />The romance in this book depended waaay too much on a past that Aria has no memory of and Hunter never mentions. Then near the end of the novel it suddenly implodes and everything is revealed at once and I just felt totally and utterly confused. You can't just do things like that. It throws people off!<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE WRITING</u>
</b><br />This is probably what saved the novel from getting a single rating. Theo's writing is actually really gorgeous, and even if Aria's voice was annoying, I cannot deny his talent. His words actually kind of flow off the page, and though his world-building is weak you can see his effort and that he really tried. His descriptions of Manhattan are gorgeous as well, and I really enjoyed the way he used his words.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>THE ENDING</u>
</b><br />Well, see, this really wasn't a surprise at all, though something tells me it was supposed to be. It was also probably supposed to be a cliffhanger, but since I didn't care for this book all that much I found myself really only mildly interested in what was going to happen next. It wasn't an awful ending, but the fact that I'd known what it was for so long really ruined it.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>WRAPUP</u>
</b><br />I will be reading the next book, although I have no idea why. Don't ask. As to would I recommend this? Honestly, no. Some people I know did love this, and I have no doubt that some of you will love it, but it just was not for me.<br /><br />FINE.<br /><br />Find more of my reviews on <a href="http://sparkles-and-lightning.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Sparkles and Lightning</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15801530510584824087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_358210292" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/358210292" />
    <a title="☕️Kimberly  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5082615-kimberly"><img alt="☕️Kimberly  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577559843p2/5082615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/358210292?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☕️Kimberly  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="☕️Kimberly  " href="/user/show/5082615-kimberly">☕️Kimberly  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer358210292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4263718381923136543">I was drawn to the gorgeous cover of Mystic City and the synopsis with its promise of a dystopian world. Theo Lawrence has a new fan. I absolutely immersed myself into the world he has created and cannot wait for the next installment in this series. From his phenomenal world building, writing style and likeable characters Lawrence completely drew me in to this fantasy world laced with paranormal elements, hatred, oppression and rebellion.<br/><br/>The tale begins when we meet Ari Rose. She is the youngest</span>
  <span id="freeText4263718381923136543" style="display:none">I was drawn to the gorgeous cover of Mystic City and the synopsis with its promise of a dystopian world. Theo Lawrence has a new fan. I absolutely immersed myself into the world he has created and cannot wait for the next installment in this series. From his phenomenal world building, writing style and likeable characters Lawrence completely drew me in to this fantasy world laced with paranormal elements, hatred, oppression and rebellion.<br /><br />The tale begins when we meet Ari Rose. She is the youngest scion of one of Mystic cities most powerful families. After a Stic overdose in which she almost dies, she wakes to find herself betrothed to Thomas Foster, the son of her parent’s sworn enemy. The upper city of Manhattan is basically divided into two political camps those who support the Roses and those who support the Fosters. When a mystic from the Depths begins a political campaign for the upcoming election, the families decided to join forces through the marriage of Ari and Thomas. Ari is confused, she cannot believe she would have tried a drug, let alone overdose and she has no memories of Thomas. Despite her concerns, her parents keep pushing the wedding plans. When Ari meets Hunter, a swoon-worthy rebel mystic who lives in the Depths, she begins to recall lost memories. Convinced he holds the key; she begins to try and regain her lost memories. The tale that unfolds is breathtaking, filled with danger, lies, actions and romance.<br /><br />When I first met Ari, I wasn’t sure what to make of her, but as she regained her memory she became surer of herself and her personality fully emerged. I ended up really liking this brave girl, as I discovered more about her and the stand she was prepared to take. She is selfless and sweet. Hunter was confident, mysterious and smexy, except when it came to Ari. From the beginning it’s apparent she is important to him and that he cares about her. I found him to be noble, protective and I became attached. Thomas seemed like a spoiled rich kid, who tried to manipulate and mold Ari. When he didn’t get his way, he tried to buy her happiness. Ari’s maid Davida was fascinating and added to the tale. Ari’s friends and those she meets in the Depth helped propel the tale and each had distinct personalities. Turk and Kiki were my favorites. I look forward to learning more about them. The people in the Rose’s circle were fascinating and it was interesting to figure out who to trust.<br /><br />The world-building and plot stole my breath away. I love world-building and Lawrence painted a Manhattan skyline that blew my mind. From the upper city to the Depths, I found the world mesmerizing. Filled with gadgets, scanners and a complex society I was in sheer heaven. I adore when a writer is able to create the world in my mind with a stroke of a pen. His attention to detail from the character’s dress to the murky tunnels delighted me. Having been to Manhattan, NY several times I was able to imagine this new world with its extreme weather and partially immersed buildings. The society was intriguing. We are slowly given details about how this dystopian world came to be, the mystic’s role in it and the caste system. I simply gobbled all of this information up. The plot was perfectly paced, with plenty of twists and turns. The romance is sweet and unfolded slowly. The characters are well fleshed out and we even see growth as Ari begins to fill in the missing pieces. I am completely enthralled with this new series and cannot wait to get my hands on book two.<br /><br />I highly recommend Mystic City to fans of dystopian, fantasy and romance. I have pre-ordered a finished copy for my book shelf. I might add this is the first, non-eBook I have ordered all year since I am trying to go digital, but I want a physical copy of this one.<br /><br />I want to thank Random House for providing this copy in exchange for my unbiased review. <a href="http://www.caffeinatedbookreviewer.com/ " rel="nofollow noopener">Kimba the Caffeinated Book Reviewer</a></span>

<div id="review_317852541" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/317852541" />
    <a title="Krystle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle"><img alt="Krystle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403921272p2/2639204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/317852541?book_show_action=true">Apr 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krystle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krystle" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle">Krystle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer317852541" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16886716182320187772">Isn’t that cover absolutely gorgeous? Gosh, I’m so in love with it. It’s even more beautiful in person! Too bad the story doesn’t live up to it.<br/><br/>Why did no one tell me this was a retelling of <i>Romeo and Juliet</i>? OHMAHGAWD! The characters even call each other Romeo and Juliet in their love letters to each other! I don’t know about you but I never saw that story as the sweeping romance it’s constantly purported to be. I take it as a cautionary tale showing the dangers of an all-consuming infatuation </span>
  <span id="freeText16886716182320187772" style="display:none">Isn’t that cover absolutely gorgeous? Gosh, I’m so in love with it. It’s even more beautiful in person! Too bad the story doesn’t live up to it.<br /><br />Why did no one tell me this was a retelling of <i>Romeo and Juliet</i>? OHMAHGAWD! The characters even call each other Romeo and Juliet in their love letters to each other! I don’t know about you but I never saw that story as the sweeping romance it’s constantly purported to be. I take it as a cautionary tale showing the dangers of an all-consuming infatuation and obsession. Don’t get me wrong, there are some very beautiful scenes but I don’t think using the story as your framework base is an excuse to drown out the plot with a heavy handed romance.<br /><br />If you’re going to set up a futuristic society that uses a location in real life, you’d better make it believable. Okay, so maybe I’ll accept the idea that mystics have always been around and have just now decided to break out into society about their existence but the severe and drastic way classes are separated does not sit well to me. How did they develop this “above ground” and below ground “depths” anyway? How did things get to this point? Why is there such a severe class distinction between the rich and the poor? I’m sorry but I never bought this. I always found it strange that this is a futuristic society but they’d still have to do “old fashioned” things like going down to a store and ordering coffee and some other things that I forgot about because I really didn’t pay that close attention to it.<br /><br />The first half was all right, interesting, although the world building was a bit rough and confusing. There was this slight mystery plot going on as to how she lost her memories and why. Then there’s this whole thing about her parents lying to her (maybe), the weird marriage she has to go through, and Davida. What’s she up to?<br /><br />Until the romance kicked in. Gross. It was so sappy and nasty. It just overshadowed everything and Aria could just burn in a fire. I’m serious. One of her direct quotes was that she found what she was born for – him. She was born for him and her whole existence was for them to be together. NASTY! Can someone say co-dependence?! I really dislike the idea that a man is everything to a woman’s existence in life. No, thank you! Not to mention their romance is so fast and heavy that I doubt they knew each other for more than a month. Ugh. Really? <i>Really</i>?<br /><br />I wanted to roll my eyes at every scene they were together. What happened to finding out what happened to you? Saving the people? Stopping the rampant drug abuse and class discrimination? No? Hah, forget that! It’s thrown out the window when the romance comes in.<br /><br />The ending made up for it. There’s a lot of action and we finally get to see the mystics’ powers in action! Fun stuff! Explosions, killings, sacrifices! Yum, yum. Didn’t expect some of the character deaths either and at least Aria gained some amount of agency in that she goes, “Oh, hey! My people are in some DEEP shizz! I gotta fix this!” which was her original goal in the first place but whatever.<br /><br />The plot is pretty predictable and I’m disappointed because this had so much potential with a beautiful cover on top but it failed terribly for me. If you’re someone who loves heavy romance in your YA novels, then I’m pretty sure you’ll lap up this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16886716182320187772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_321534932" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/321534932" />
    <a title="Soumi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6833452-soumi"><img alt="Soumi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1440767658p2/6833452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/321534932?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Soumi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Soumi" href="/user/show/6833452-soumi">Soumi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=books-i-reviewed">books-i-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6833452-soumi?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer321534932" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13312613975897761377">There have been many books published in recent days as a blend of X-Men in dystopian world. But in case of Mystic City, it was unexpectedly gorgeous. The story was truly gripping and intensely affecting afterwards.<br/> <br/>In a distant futuristic tale, where most of the Manhattan resides underwater and the upper city is run by energy drawn from mystics. Aria Rose, daughter of one of the two most powerful family of city, doesn't remember a thing about her past before she overdosed on Stic, a drug mad of </span>
  <span id="freeText13312613975897761377" style="display:none">There have been many books published in recent days as a blend of X-Men in dystopian world. But in case of Mystic City, it was unexpectedly gorgeous. The story was truly gripping and intensely affecting afterwards.<br /> <br />In a distant futuristic tale, where most of the Manhattan resides underwater and the upper city is run by energy drawn from mystics. Aria Rose, daughter of one of the two most powerful family of city, doesn't remember a thing about her past before she overdosed on Stic, a drug mad of mystic energy, or at least it’s what she was told. Now she is engaged to a boy she doesn't remember having feelings for, with flashes of another boy in her memories. The day she met Hunter, a rebel mystic, everything around her changes and she realized he holds the key to her past.<br />I admit I had very mixed feeling about the book before I started it, and now I feel it was a mind blowing that I finished the book within a 3 hours train journey because I couldn't let it go. The writing was beautiful, vivid and I loved the way the author described a divided Manhattan, mystics those live in Depths of city and the controlling class harvesting on mystic power. <br /><br />There is a certain kind of attraction flamed between them in a way that is not quite explainable . The romance was described in a cute way, not your boy meets girls and lightning strikes, rather it was something beyond magical. With a rebellion ignited and political turmoil, a love blossoms however it was pretty much predictable that Hunter is the one Aria fell in love with, not Thomas, the boy she is engaged to. It was a dystopian forbidden love between the daughter of the most powerful and controlling man of Manhattan and a rebel mystic whose mother is a worthy opponent in upcoming election.<br /><br />Both the lead characters are developed well. Aria is desperate to find answers for her memory loss because the story her family fed her was definitely not believable. And Hunter was desperate to keep her safe at any cost. Finally when a moment came, both of them fought against all the odds. It’s needless to say Hunter is one of the fictional boys I recently developed a crush for. What unexpected is Aria because I never thought her to be the tough as she really is, and by her bravery she caught me off guard. <br /><br />Other than the romance part, the book has many unpredictable things which left me by surprise but I’m not going to disclose then in this review. After finishing the book in a single breath and finally when I exhaled, one word came out of my mouth “Wow….. I’m blown away by Mystic City.”<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13312613975897761377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1301495089" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1301495089" />
    <a title="Melody (theliteraryowl)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5586723-melody-theliteraryowl"><img alt="Melody (theliteraryowl)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567423626p2/5586723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1301495089?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melody (theliteraryowl)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melody (theliteraryowl)" href="/user/show/5586723-melody-theliteraryowl">Melody (theliteraryowl)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9782266231923" href="/book/show/18611949-mystic-city">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5586723-melody-theliteraryowl?shelf=tbr">tbr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5586723-melody-theliteraryowl?shelf=books-that-i-own">books-that-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5586723-melody-theliteraryowl?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5586723-melody-theliteraryowl?shelf=annoying-protagonist">annoying-protagonist</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1301495089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13748531898244056157">Ugh. Where to start ? This book is quite ridiculous. Seriously. It is a rather good distraction for summer, but nothing more. It's crazy how everything is so predictable. The main protagonist is plain and such a stereotype, there is no character development and that bothered me a lot. The author uses in Mystic City devices that are all overly used in literature (especially in YA/dystopias) and there is no surprise whatsoever.<br/><br/>The main idea of the story is rather interesting though: a sort of floo</span>
  <span id="freeText13748531898244056157" style="display:none">Ugh. Where to start ? This book is quite ridiculous. Seriously. It is a rather good distraction for summer, but nothing more. It's crazy how everything is so predictable. The main protagonist is plain and such a stereotype, there is no character development and that bothered me a lot. The author uses in Mystic City devices that are all overly used in literature (especially in YA/dystopias) and there is no surprise whatsoever.<br /><br />The main idea of the story is rather interesting though: a sort of flooded New-York city where wealthy people live The Aeries (the city in the sky) and poor people live in The Depths + people with superpowers (the mystics/the poor) but that's it. The fact that the story focuses more on the "love story" aspect rather than the dystopia/fantasy aspect annoyed me a lot. I would have loved to read more about the political aspect of the book, the author could have written such a great book then but nope, it focused on Aria and her "love turmoils" and I don't really care for romance, what I want is action, amazing world-building and an interesting female lead so I was really disappointed when I closed the book, the fact that the character stays the same from beginning to end annoyed me somewhat and I just hated the romance so much and everything was so predictable I knew what was coming. I feel like I'm super harsh with this book but I just can't deal with it. The writing style was good -though rather simple- and I felt like the author knew what he was doing and where he wanted to go with his story so that was a good point and that's why I'm giving this book 3/5 stars (if it were not for the writing style I would probably have rated it 2/5 stars.) <br />I'm really sorry but this book wasn't for me and I won't read the sequel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13748531898244056157" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3829694-mlpmom-book-reviewer?shelf=arc-book-read">arc-book-read</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer16326245698458313217"> Let me simply start by saying, the cover on this book is breathtaking and this is one time that you can completely judge a book by its cover.<br/><br/>I was sucked right into Aria's world. The prologue was so compelling that it left me eagerly turning the pages to get to the first chapter. I wanted to learn more about Aria and the mystery boy that had stolen her heart.<br/><br/>And while I can't go into any kind of detail about names, just know that this was a tale worthy of Romeo and Juliet. I absolutely loved th</span>
  <span id="freeText16326245698458313217" style="display:none"> Let me simply start by saying, the cover on this book is breathtaking and this is one time that you can completely judge a book by its cover.<br /><br />I was sucked right into Aria's world. The prologue was so compelling that it left me eagerly turning the pages to get to the first chapter. I wanted to learn more about Aria and the mystery boy that had stolen her heart.<br /><br />And while I can't go into any kind of detail about names, just know that this was a tale worthy of Romeo and Juliet. I absolutely loved the star cross lovers theme this whole story had going for it.<br /><br />The details for Aria's life and world were so well done and crafted. Not everything was explained about her world but just enough that it left you with a good idea of what was going on and a beautofil description of what it looked like.<br /><br />I am so torn, I want to tell you so much more but I really don't want to ruin the story for you. I hate spoilers!<br /><br />But Aria is a great strong character, in fact this book is full of them. You will love all of the characters, some you will even love to hate and despise.<br /><br />If you are looking for something different, something a little fantasy and a little dystopian with lots of romance (but not over the top or the whole focus of the story) you really need to pick this one up and read it. </span>

<div id="review_1026790175" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1026790175" />
    <a title="Samantha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10067920-samantha"><img alt="Samantha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590018789p2/10067920.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1026790175?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha" href="/user/show/10067920-samantha">Samantha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1026790175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer919662395184425826">This story had a lot of potential, but it got lost on the way. <br/><br/>LIKES: <br/>It had a very interesting premise. Two "mafia" type families. Mysterious memory loss. Star-crossed lovers. Futuristic New York City. What's not to love, right?!<br/><br/>DISLIKES: <br/>The setting was not properly worked out. It was set sometime in the future when global warming has taken over and people with mystical powers have made themselves known. Everyone can pay for items through their fingerprints, not needing to carry money. But tex</span>
  <span id="freeText919662395184425826" style="display:none">This story had a lot of potential, but it got lost on the way. <br /><br />LIKES: <br />It had a very interesting premise. Two "mafia" type families. Mysterious memory loss. Star-crossed lovers. Futuristic New York City. What's not to love, right?!<br /><br />DISLIKES: <br />The setting was not properly worked out. It was set sometime in the future when global warming has taken over and people with mystical powers have made themselves known. Everyone can pay for items through their fingerprints, not needing to carry money. But texting and tweeting was still referenced. What? 100-150 years in the future and we are still tweeting? I think not.<br /><br />The love story was not believable. Not to mention that the male lead had no kind of continuity. He would act and talk one way in one chapter, and completely different in the next. I could not get a beat on his personality. <br /><br />The magic system was not explained and was completely random. There was no method to the madness. <br /><br />You can see the twists coming from a mile away. The "big twist" is easily seen from the readers perspective in the first 10 or so chapters, and it still takes the main character until the last 50 pages to figure it out herself....<br /><br />OVERALL, the story had a lot of potential, but didn't live up to it. I do not plan on continuing this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="919662395184425826" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_371406233" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/371406233" />
    <a title="Tammie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3506989-tammie"><img alt="Tammie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604938056p2/3506989.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/371406233?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tammie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tammie" href="/user/show/3506989-tammie">Tammie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=trilogy">trilogy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3506989-tammie?shelf=series-abandoned">series-abandoned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer371406233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5707834330090157017">I was really looking forward to reading Mystic City, especially when the description referenced Blade Runner, but unfortunately this book fell flat. I liked the idea behind it and everything, but couldn't help but compare the whole memory wipe scenario to another book I read called Renegade by J.A. Souders that did it better. And back to that Blade Runner reference, I didn't really see anything in this book that resembled Blade Runner. <br/><br/>I think my biggest problem with the book was how infuriating</span>
  <span id="freeText5707834330090157017" style="display:none">I was really looking forward to reading Mystic City, especially when the description referenced Blade Runner, but unfortunately this book fell flat. I liked the idea behind it and everything, but couldn't help but compare the whole memory wipe scenario to another book I read called Renegade by J.A. Souders that did it better. And back to that Blade Runner reference, I didn't really see anything in this book that resembled Blade Runner. <br /><br />I think my biggest problem with the book was how infuriatingly stupid Aria is sometimes, and Hunter too. There is a whole scene where she and Hunter should be escaping out the window and they just sit there and chat until they get caught. And why in the world doesn't she ever lock the door? Hunter has these awesome powers but conveniently doesn't think to use them most of the time so that they get caught and we have the whole "How are they going to get out of this?" scenario. <br /><br />I also think the book would have been more interesting if we had gotten to know more about Thomas and his motivations. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5707834330090157017" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NQigvy4XNSIt18YiCOHBCYF7qU4D9e820pyTTeSbxFA4xA+Glmnh/KjTF25neoD8kc7mLDcWwXwGnW0EyPmFjg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gYCu7e/TtFjMoA/nsVe13a2z2H+Qw1+4yLqcqBT51CuMTAHUV61ghkmk3qvezPQovQaXHaQgcfIcu2LhOJuV9Q==')})
  }
//]]>
